<gmapID>0x808fec0500740ed7:0xda6996f0e89ac19d</gmapID><Rating>1</Rating><user_id>101260180476374892962<//user_id><user_name>Karthik M</user_name>< text>
This review concerns my recent experience with the Owner/Manager. This is one of the many car wash/gas stations in Dublin... I used to quite often get my car washed here...most times it was convenient on the way to freeway entrance. Sometimes their machine used to breakdown, and they would take a few minutes to come and restart it...no big deal so far.

However I had quite a bad experience while I was about to get into the car wash. For some reason it appears their machine malfunctioned, and the car in front of me drove away...while I was still cleaning my wheels. The owner came out and started yelling at me to remove my car from the line, telling me others were waiting (There was no one behind me at that time). I told him to give me time enough to put the brush away and he basically told me "Move it now or do you want me to shut the machine down!". Uggh...had I not paid for my wash already I would have left then!

I find this quite appalling...Mr owner...if you happen to read my post, please understand if your machine malfunctions, there is no point is taking out the frustration on your customer...it does not help the situation, if anything yelling at me for your machine breakdown just turns me away!

Anyway I guess there is sufficient competition for car washes in the area, and personally I see no need to patronize this business again.</text>

< Review>
I often travel for work. Being a vegan this is can be challenging at times., but San Diego thankfully has no shortage of vegan options. Don't let that cause you to miss Rollin Roots. I checked them out because they were the closest option and I really lucked out.

The Rich Gal sandwich is hands down one of the all time top 5 sandwiches I've ever had. It seemed expensive, but the sandwich is enormous. It's enough to feed 2 people. I had half for lunch and the second half for lunch the next day.

Don't miss this place.<//Review>

It was my first time eating at a Waba Grill and I didn't even know this location was even there. It looked brand new and not many people were in there.
I had the steak veggie bowl with brown rice and it was OKAY. The typical super sweet teriyaki beef on a bed of brown rice with steamed veggies.

<Resp>None< /Resp><rate>4< /rate><Review>Lunch Specials!

Those two words when put together just brings happiness. I came here with a group for Friday lunch and it wasn't busy. Their restaurant is clean and well decorated, it was pretty fancy. Luckily, they do not charge ridiculous prices unlike other fancy restaurants. We were greeted by a friendly server and immediately upon getting the menu, I looked straight for the lunch specials. All their lunch specials were $7.25 unless you got seafood then it was a $1 more. I ordered their mongolian chicken with fried rice. I love how you can choose the rice (brown, white, fried rice) at no additional charge :)

It also comes with a small salad and crispy wonton strips for starters. The lunch special was decently large.They gave a good amount of beef and rice. I liked the mongolian beef. The beef was chewy, not too firm and it had a nice spicy kick to it. The fried rice was okay, not really any flavor to it but it did come with peas and carrots. I did notice that their food isn't really greasy which is a huge plus for me! Overall I was surprised and happy with the meal. Our server was friendly and was nice enough to split the bill with 3 different credit cards with no fuss. They definitely get points for no attitude and accepting credit cards!

Great lunch spot and seems like a good overall place for any other time as well.<//Review><GmapID>0x808f9e7062e5c9d9:0xf591829b87324273<//GmapID>< Date>

< review>
Authentic, delicious and affordable. Highly recommended!! Our top 2 Chinese restaurants in San Mateo/Burlingame.

Was browsing for new places for dinner in San Mateo. Found this to be near where we were for our chiro session.

Reached around 7pm and the eatery only had a couple tables occupied. We were promptly seated by a really friendly server.

Picked Seafood Pan Fried Noodles, Hot & Sour soup and Sweet and Sour Pork.

The Hot & Sour soup came first in a huge bowl. A little worried on whether we were able to finish it initially, but after taking the first sip, we were hooked. It was so good especially so for a cool evening. Before we know it, the bowl was empty.

The Seafood Pan Fried Noodles was done in a Hong Kong style, which is somewhat dry and crispy noodles. I must say the dish was done to perfection. It had a good amount of sauce that makes it so yummy with the ingredients yet not too much to turn the crispy noodles soggy too quickly. It had vegetables (done really well), prawns, squid and fish (though we felt the fish didn't seem that fresh) everything else was awesome.

Sweet and Sour Pork arrived shortly after the noodles. It is usually best paired with rice but the noodles worked well for us. The pork was also absolutely yummy, loved every bite! The taste was great, was perhaps lacking of some pineapples.

Service was great. We love how attentive the server was and how efficient they were. It was a very pleasant experience.

By the time we were done with our meal, the place started to fill up.

I really enjoyed the food. It has now clinched top spot in Chinese eatery list.< /review>

<UserId.>112717194313401631895<//UserId.>< Review>
The service, professionalism and care at Platinum Collision Center were all superb.  The entire staff, from the receptionist to the owner (Tom), consistently provided excellent service beyond my expectations.

I had a minor fender-bender on my Tesla and needed to have the rear bumper repaired.
The estimate process was quick and easy.  Jackie meets you at the front desk in the most friendly and helpful manner.  Veronica assesses the damage thoroughly and provides the estimate.  They set up an immediate date for my repair and even made arrangements for me to get  a rental car at the site.  All I had to do was drop off my car.

Jhann, the manager, keeps you informed about the entire repair process.  He is very knowledgeable and experienced.  He works with the insurance company to get the repairs covered and completed as quickly as possible.  When my insurance company, State Farm, became less than willing to cover the necessary repairs, Jhann effectively communicated with me and State Farm to explain each itemized cost.  In the end, all repairs were beautifully done and covered with a lifetime warranty.

I am extremely satisfied with my experience at Platinum.   Thank you for the excellent service.  I highly recommend Platinum Collision Center in Eastvale!</Review>

My bill ended up being $1,022 higher than the $2,248 stated in the "Binding Moving Estimate" I received. That's almost 50% more - pretty hefty. After the move from Oregon to DC was done, I looked at the paperwork again, because of some damage to my furniture. It raised some serious questions. I thought the price increase wasn't justified, so I sent Golden Valley Van Line emails with the questions I had. I sent an email on December 12, 2018. I then tried again on January 5 and again on January 19, 2019. I never received an answer. By now I feel scammed.
I wasn't in Oregon when Golden Valley picked up my stuff at a friend's house. At the time of pickup the company representative claimed that it was much more than what I had estimated. He charged me $672 more. It was a take it or leave it kind of deal with my friend wanting my stuff out of her garage, and I wasn't there, so I agreed. When my stuff arrived, I did the math and found out that it was just 9 cubic feet more - kind of a steep surcharge. At arrival I was told that the large truck couldn't park in front of my house, so I would have to pay $350 for a shuttle. The surcharge for such a shuttle is in the contract. What's not in the contract is that the "shuttle" seemed to have been the main transporter. There was no large 18-wheeler outside the city, as the company representative had told me the day before and then again that day. The van and trailer combination that did arrive with my furniture had another client's furniture in it, and the guys told me they were in a hurry to deliver it to another city that day.

So, to sum it up:
Pros: It started outas one of the lowest priced offers (but of course it didn't stay that way). The furniture was well packaged with thick blankets all around. The guys delivering it were pretty careful and handled everything well.
Cons: One rail on my bed was damaged and my washer apparently dropped at one point. I feel cheated out of $1,022. Communication was terrible.

The last three emails being ignored was not the first time communications with "Christine S." completely dropped (there is no last name on any of the paperwork - interesting - I mean, social media is different, but there is no last name in ANY of her communications, not even the contract or receipt). When I tried to arrange delivery, I didn't hear from her for weeks and then only got phony excuses. When I complained about the surcharge for the van because the 18-wheeler couldn't get to my house, I was told that I was being "difficult" to work with. Same kind of take-it-or-leave-it deal, only this time with my stuff in the company's possession. At delivery the company representative immediately threatened to leave if I wouldn't sign the papers and handed over the money first thing. When I asked for a receipt from him he refused and didn't even want to tell me his full name (same deal as with Christine S., remember?).

Long story short, this California branch of Golden Valley Van Line is NOT a trustworthy partner I would ever recommend for your move.<//text>

< Text>
Please take the time to read this. I have vowed to be better at writing reviews as I depend on them myself so often. I am not one to get my kicks from bashing a company either but this needs to be known. PLEASE, do yourself a favor and just use another company that doesn't bait and switch you.

Now that we have our stuff loaded into our new house, I feel I can finally write this. Our dealings with Golden Valley Van Lines began about 8 weeks ago when they called after I filled out an online quote request for our move from Seattle to Phoenix. I was overwhelmed with emails and phone calls before I finally received a call from Diane with GVVL. She immediately made me feel comfortable with them being a local company and in business for so many years. I knew after the phone call that they were the ones we would use.

My wife then spent a good hour with her on the phone going over each room and what we had. We are a typical family of 4 so after all the big furniture, they have some algorithm they use to determine your cubic ft volume. Our bid was for $5200ish.  This was also less than the few other bids we received so I called Diane myself. I asked if she would please come to our house and verify. She again explained to me that this would be the number as long as we don't add anymore furniture etc. I told her I was worried about a change on moving day but she put those worries to rest again explaining their experience level. So, I put down a 20% deposit to secure the date ($1,000).

I got a call from Christine a few days before the move and she asked if they could deliver earlier than planned as the truck would go from our house, directly to Az. We had to scramble around to get someone there to unlock the door for us but we were able to make it happen. It wasn't until the movers showed up that I realized we were in serious trouble. They were clearly a separate company who had been brokered by these scammers and their new bid was for $9800. He said we had more than the 1200 cubic feet that we were quoted. In fact, maybe double. Not to mention that although our estimate include blanketing and taping furniture, it apparently also needs to be shrink wrapped, which was not included. Long story short, it was a terrible experience and if I had more time to worry about this, I would take them to small claims court. They didn't know where our stuff even was 3 days after they left. Christine lied and said she never told us it was going straight down. The movers on the Az side were rude and careless. Just a downright awful experience.

Find another moving company!!< /Text>

I have moved 17 times in the past 22 years. Multi state trips and never had any missing items or damage, until Golden Valley Van Lines came along! Started with a phone call from Eddy who told us about being a family owned business, not like ‚Äúthe other guys‚Äù. The move was from Cheyenne WY to Seattle. We were told that our household goods would be stored in Seattle as they had a facility there. On to the move, pick-up day came and went before we got a call that their truck broke down outside Denver and they  would arrive early the next day. In the afternoon the following day they showed up with a Penske truck. Their late arrival cost me 2 more days as I had to reschedule the carpet cleaners and others that were coming. We were told that all goods would be delivered within 7-10 days upon notice. I rented a home in the Seattle area and called them 10 days prior to move in date. The day is was to arrive we were told it would be the following weekend (another 7 days), but window was sometime between Saturday and Monday and they would call closer to delivery. We were now in a home with no furniture, dishes or anything. We called Christine (owners daughter) on Friday to ask what the delievery window looked like. (3 day weekend and grandchild only 250 miles a.way). Christine said to go, delivery would be on Tuesday. We left town and received a call from the movers that they would arrive Saturday morning. Explained what we had been told and told them we would be back on Monday. Driver stated that they could not deliver on our street and we would have to pay a $600 transfer fee. I explained that our street does not have load restrictions. (The previous owner parked his semi with 53‚Äô box truck in front of the house during his lunch hour everyday) We were also told that payment had to be cash or postal money order at time of stop or delivery would be taken back. When movers arrived with the U-haul truck the driver refused cash and told me I had 30 minutes to get a postal money order or they would leave. Now we were toold they were a contractor from NJ who was hired to hual our things from Denver. All large items in the move were damaged. Filed the claims with CSI in March of last year. Inputed weights were changed in the 9 months it took to process the claim and my leather topped desk with broken top only qualified for 25% damage by weight because it was ONLY cosmetic and still worked as a desk.  They tried their best to wear us down. Final check, which didn‚Äôt cover one of the items, was received in late December. They refused to discuss the extra  $600 transfer fee. Worst.Move.Ever
While it is true they are family owned, the are only in reality a ‚ÄúBroker‚Äù for movers that are looking for work. Great communications until the goods were loaded then BOOM, hard time getting thru to anyone or to call you back. Would NOT recommend them for anything but lip service.<//Review>

<gmapID>0x80c29e97f5233bc1:0xbc42873efccea9d4<//gmapID><review>TLDR - They weren't too expensive and eventually got me (most of) my things. They did probably $500 worth of damage/theft, but hopefully were cheap enough to offset that, hence the 3 stars.

First off, these are the guys who say they're in Colorado, or perhaps wherever you happen to be moving from. A guy named Mark called me from a local Colorado number and everything, but they are based in Cali. He says his "Jewish guilt" will keep him from ignoring you if there are any problems, and that a guy who reported two tvs missing, the owner just "bought him two tvs, because that's the kind of guy he is."

Well, they stole my step stool and broke two expensive floor lamps, and he and customer service aren't replying. My $1200+ bicycle was precariously perched-- its fenders are damaged, but hopefully that's all it is. And then there was this circus:

- Started moving on a Wednesday and was told my things would be there Thursday (Denver to SLC). This was huge, as you will notice most companies, including this one, will tell you something like 3-10 days for a move of this distance. It was a big reason I went with them.
- I get there Wednesday at no small physical expense.. cleaning up and moving out and driving 8 hours the same day they picked up my things (and the day they broke lamp #1 by knocking it over where they set it down in the hallway-- $200+ to replace). Oh yeah, they assured me they would pay for it. That would be a lie.
- I get called late Thursday that they will be there in an hour to unload. They did not show. No call. No one is answering. Fun, right? Are my things burning in a ditch?
- I call Friday morning. Apparently the number on their truck doesn't match their permit or something. They had to pay a fine and fix it. I was told when they'd be arriving later that day.
- No call, no show, again. Fortunately I was able to get a hold of the driver this time, who told me that because he was under 21 he was not able to drive that truck in the state of Utah. They would be flying a driver out to make the delivery Sunday. Yes, seriously.
- My things are delivered Sunday. Thankfully. I started a job on Monday and was really hoping to have this taken care of beforehand. I'm still unpacking as a result, but at least I didn't have to miss any work.
- I was given a claim form for my damaged things.. But very important-- everything has to be written on the form you sign that says your things were delivered. They will not tell you this so that you won't be able to make a claim (neither customer service nor the movers told me, as I recall). But it doesn't matter as the basic option only gets you $.60/lb per item, pretty standard, which is nothing. You are trusting a company to do the right thing and take care of your things, and this one falls a bit short.

So there ya go.. Some people would give 1 star based on this experience, but I try to be objective.. Could've been better, could've been worse. I will give someone else a shot next time around.< /review>< Resp>

And every time you call this place you end up getting transferred around to way way way too many people - all while being given excuses & very little help.  Since I purchased the car, I have met several people who had similar experiences wit this dealership.
Thankfully Mazda makes good vehicles and I have not had any problems with the actual car itself - only the shady antics of the sales & service teams at Culver City Mazda. They pretend, and even try in some instances, to be helpful - but frequently do not follow through, giving excuse after excuse why they cant help. It is stressful, deceptive and totally unnecessary.< /Review></record></dataset><record>

< review>
My experience with Culver City Mazda has been very positive, starting from the time you arrive for your appointment till you leave. You are greeted upon arrival, and told how long (5-10 minutes) your wait will be till a service advisor checks your car in. After check-in, it is very pleasant to sit in their waiting area, have excellent coffee (and/or donuts), and read the newspaper, or browse the Internet on your phone or laptop. Culver City Mazda is moving to a new customer management software, so I was greeted by an advisor with everything on their iPad. I didn't have to wait at the service desk like I did before. Nice to see.

When the servicing was complete, someone came and found me (rather than announce on the PA), to let me know that the car was ready. Plus my car got a complimentary car wash!! Also a nice touch.

Overall, a pleasant experience. Happy to be a Mazda customer.<//review>

< Review>
While shopping for a Mazda CX-5, someone in the business recommended that I meet with Tony, the fleet manager at the Culver City Mazda location. When I made an appointment to meet with him, he blew me off and had me work with one of his associates, which was fine because I know they‚Äôre busy. I met with Rosie, who truly created a great experience. She was professional, knowledgeable, and nice to work with. After two test drives, I was ready to buy the car. I found a better deal at a different location, but because Rosie had put time and effort into the sale, I gave her an opportunity to earn the commission by countering the deal. She said she could beat the price by $300 and threw in a due bill for Apple CarPlay and some curtesy rubber mats. After inspecting the car, which was excellently detailed, I was ready to pull the trigger and sign some paperwork. I met with Richard, the Finance Manager of F&I. Initially, I found him to also be professional and courteous, but he quickly revealed himself as a misogynist who attempted to take advantage of me as a woman and first time car buyer. He quoted me at 6% interest rate, which you know is absurd if you‚Äôre familiar with how financing works. I was putting down more than half of the car‚Äôs worth and have a fairly decent credit score (680 with trans union and 733 with Equifax). He repeatedly called me ‚Äúsweetie‚Äù and told me that there was nothing he could do to reduce the interest rate and that only the bank can do that, which was clearly untrue. After telling him that I was leaving, he left to ‚Äúget approval‚Äù from the fleet manager to lower my interest rate. I thought only the banks could do that? He then gave me an interest rate just under 4%. When I told him that was still ridiculous and I was leaving, he said ‚Äúsweetie, you just don‚Äôt understand how all of this works.‚Äù They clearly were not going to give me a reasonable interest rate, so I asked about leasing instead because I know that Mazda has a 0% interest rate for leasing. Tony and Richard gave me the worst quote I‚Äôve ever heard of in my life. Putting $6,000 down to pay $300 a month for a MAZDA is absurd. They very obviously did not want my business, so I left. The only thing I feel bad about is the work that Rosie put in. Yesterday I found the same car for the same price at Galpin Mazda. They offered me a 2.4% interest rate and I gave my business to them instead. Claudia Campos was my salesperson and she was phenomenal, as was the finance manager Paris. It was a smooth process and I drove off the lot last night.

TLDR: Do not buy your car from Culver City. Go to Galpin Mazda instead. The Fleet Manager, Tony, at Culver City was rude and the Financial Manager, Richard was the most misogynistic person I‚Äôve ever dealt with professionally. They will take advantage of you if you‚Äôre a woman and they think you don‚Äôt know what you‚Äôre doing. I do not recommend giving them your business.< /Review>

<date>1470934348438<//date><rating>5</rating><Text>I am usually very skeptical of car dealers. I always tend to question their honesty and get annoyed by all the pressure put on me by the sales people.

I was in the market for a brand new car. Previous to visiting Culver City Mazda I had visited many car dealerships of various brands to narrow down my choices including Mazda in Van Nuys. After my visit to the Van Nuys Mazda I was very nervous about dealing with Mazda salespeople. I felt as though there was a lot of dishonesty and contradiction in statements made by the dealership.

I decided to visit Culver City Mazda because of a great offer I received by email. I then made an appointment with Lee. Driving in to Culver City Mazda I saw the small delarship due to construction. I immediately thought this experience will probably be a disaster. To my surprise everyone was very organized. Pulling in we immediately were greeted by someone who took the car I was in and parked it for us. Lee then came outside soon after to greet us and introduce us to Michael who sat us down and discussed the exact car I wanted. He was extremely knowledgeable in all of Mazda cars. I was very impressed. After discussing the type of car, Michael drove us to the other lot to pick out the car. Michael was very friendly and easy to have a conversation with.

Now that I had picked out the car it was time to talk numbers with Lee. Like Michael, Lee was very easy to talk to and addressed all of my concerns in pricing. To make a long story short he wasn't going to let us leave without my new car. I believe Lee was honest in the numbers presented and did what he could to work out a very fair deal for the car that both him and I could agree on.

Next was the financing department. I met with Will who went over all the paperwork with me so that I could understand exactly what I was signing for. He too was very friendly and knowledgeable.

Overall I have to say this dealership was one of the best I have ever been to or purchased a car from. There is almost a family type vibe between all the workers making for a very enjoyable experience for their customers. I definitely recommend this dealership to anyone who is looking to purchase a Mazda. I will more than likely be returning to this dealership when it's time for my next car.</Text><pics>None</pics>< Resp>
